Sports

Shanghai's First

Joint Middle School Sports Meet - Day One

National Women's Long Jump Record│Zhang Pingxian│4.30 Meters

│Yesterday's Winners│

Group　Men's A Jinan│Men's B Nanyang Model│Women's Dongya

Individual　Men's A Chen Xingpei│Men's B Deng Yingyuan│Women Zhang Pingxian

The Shanghai First Joint Middle School Sports Meet, organized by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, opened yesterday afternoon at the China Athletic Field on Rue du Père Huc. Over 30 schools and over 500 male and female athletes participated, and the stands were packed with spectators, making it a grand occasion. The entire group first paraded around the field, followed by the opening ceremony, and then the sports began. Six men's and women's finals were held. In the women's long jump, Ms. Zhang Pingxian of Dongya set a new national record with 4.30 meters. Today is the second day, and even better results are expected.

Opening Ceremony

After the parade, the male and female athletes from each school stood in a single line facing the podium. Amidst the music of the military band, the solemn and grand unprecedented event slowly began, and the ceremony was held in the following order: (1) Everyone stands at attention; (2) Music is played; (3) The Party Song is sung; (4) The national flag and the portrait of the Premier are given the highest respect; (5) Chairman Xu Peihuang respectfully reads the Premier's will; (6) Silence; (7) Chairman Xu Peihuang reports; (8) Representative Yu Hongjun, the President of the Association, delivers a speech; (9) Tong Xingbai, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivers a speech; (10) Honorary Instructor Chu Fuchen delivers a speech; (11) Guest Zhu Yingpeng delivers a speech; (12) Ceremony concludes.

Chairman Xu Peihuang's Report　He briefly stated that today is the first time that the city is holding a joint middle school sports meet. The main purpose is to popularize physical education in middle schools and to test the level of physical education in middle schools. The number of athletes participating this time is 519, including 328 in the men's A group, 98 in the men's B group, and 93 women. The nature of each school includes two provincial schools, two national schools, five municipal schools, three private university-affiliated middle schools, and eighteen private university-affiliated middle schools that have not been registered, which can be divided into (1) public and private registered schools; (2) middle schools that have not been registered but have completed registration procedures. Finally, he thanked the China National Amateur Athletic Federation for providing the venue, and the support of various bureaus and sports experts, as well as the Upper Middle and Dongya Boy Scouts for maintaining order.

President Zhang Yuejun's Speech　Mayor Zhang's representative, Yu Hongjun, briefly stated that he was ordered by the mayor to attend the grand opening ceremony of the first joint middle school sports meet. The public and private male and female students participating this time will use their skills developed through daily training to show their abilities. Strong physiques developed on this day will be used for serving society and the country in the future. Promoting sports can (1) cultivate a spirit of self-discipline; (2) cultivate a sense of discipline; (3) compete fairly through legitimate means. He hopes that all athletes will develop their individual sports and sporting virtues and advance with each year.

Party Headquarters Tong Xingbai's Speech　He briefly stated that physical education is related to the future of each individual, as well as the survival of society and the country. While exploring intellectual and moral education, we must not forget to study physical education. Physical education is the foundation of the three educations. Mr. Sun Yat-sen's greatest expectation is the development of the spirit of the Chinese nation, starting with morality, and physical education occupies the center of morality. There are two essential meanings to studying physical education: (1) permanent self-cultivation; (2) universal development.

Honorary Instructor Chu Fuchen's Speech　Mr. Chu briefly stated that people call our country an old and sick man, which is painful to think about. If each individual can pay attention to physical education, they can create a promising country of youth. He himself has been sick since middle age, but even now that he is nearly sixty years old, he does not feel old, because of the effect of exercising for one hour every morning for decades. If individuals do this, and all the people in the country can follow suit, then our country will be healthy for everyone.

Guest Zhu Yingpeng's Speech　Mr. Zhu briefly stated that when we stand shoulder to shoulder with Westerners, there is a clear difference in height and strength. The reason why Westerners are strong is because they have been constantly training for thousands of years, which has allowed them to maintain the physique of their original ethnic group. People in our country have placed physical education outside of all things in life. This kind of misconception has created a nation that is small and weak today. Now we must strive for progress so that we can be as strong and healthy as the tall and large Western nations.

(1) 50-meter Semifinals (Women) (2) 100-meter Semifinals (Men's Groups A and B) (3) Shot Put Final (Men's Groups A and B, Women) (4) 100-meter Semifinals (Women) (5) 400-meter Semifinals (Men's Groups A and B) (6) High Hurdles Semifinals (Men's Group A) (7) Javelin Final (Men's Group A, Women) (8) 200-meter Semifinals (Men's Groups A and B, Women) (9) Triple Jump Final (Men's Group A) (10) 400-meter Intermediate Hurdles Semifinals (Men's Group A) (11) 800-meter Preliminary (Men's Groups A and B) (12) 1600-meter Relay Final (Men's Group A) (13) 400-meter Relay Final (Women)

Outstanding Achievements

Yesterday, there were seven preliminary events for men and women, three final events for Men's Group A, two final events for Men's Group B, and one final event for Women. The results were excellent. In particular, Chen Xingpei of Pudong achieved 4 minutes and 39.8 seconds in the 1500 meters, and Qu Junyuan of Wusong Aquatic Products achieved 5.82 meters in the long jump. These results are rare for middle school students. Furthermore, the top three in the women's long jump all broke the National Games record, which is especially noteworthy.

Women's Long Jump Breaks National Record

The women's long jump final was an outstanding achievement of yesterday's meet. The first place, Zhang Pingxian, and the second place, Qian Hangsu, both broke Wu Meixian's record of 4 meters in the National Games. The third place, Chen Yunqing's 4 meters, equaled Wu Meixian's 4 meters. The fifth place was Yang Zhiren of Southeast, with a score equal to the fourth place, both being 3.96 meters. However, due to the new rule of no ties, another final was held, and Yang failed. Xia Fenlu scored 4.01 meters, which can be said to be fortunate and unfortunate. Yesterday's women's long jump results were particularly good. It is a pity that the sky was already darkening at the time, making running and jumping difficult; otherwise, the results would have been even better. There were twenty participants in the competition.

Women's 50-meter Also Sets New Record

In the women's 50-meter preliminary, the first place in the third group, Zhang Pingxian of East Asia, achieved 7.3 seconds, which is also equal to the new national record. Sun Guiyun's national record for 50 meters is 7.3 seconds, and Cao Hanhua's record in Malaya is 7.3 seconds. However, Wu Meixian of Harbin achieved a score of 7 seconds in the Northeast Four Provinces Joint Sports Meet.

1500-meter Celebrated Athlete Wins Title

In the 1500-meter final, fifty-six people started. With the sound of the gun, everyone sprinted forward. The track was crowded and chaotic, a magnificent scene. After one lap, the celebrated athlete Chen Xingpei chased quickly and led the pack, his demeanor very relaxed. Qiu Lingru followed him, about ten yards behind. After the second and third laps, Chen still remained in the lead, but he did not fall behind either. The rest of the competitors followed one after another, trailing by about half a lap. In the last lap, everyone strove forward. Chen Xingpei was always in the lead, and he finally won the championship with a time of 4 minutes and 39.8 seconds. The result was especially remarkable, not only rare in middle schools but also rarely seen in universities. The second place, Qiu Lingru, was still about ten yards behind.

Local News

Urgent Telegram from the Municipal Executive Committee

Abolish All Unequal Treaties

The Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party issued a telegram yesterday, stating, "To all provincial and municipal party headquarters, all special party headquarters, all general branches, all national newspapers, and all legal entities across the country: The essential element for the establishment of a nation lies first in the complete sovereignty, and the freedom of national development requires the advocacy of independence. Today, the imperialists, through unequal treaties, infringe upon our sovereignty, obstruct our advocacy, oppress us at will for eighty years, and also harbor bandits, hinder our security, and provide aid and weapons to prolong our Red disaster. Their desire to keep our nation in a perpetual state of danger and our people in a state of weakness is evident. Now, the new Chinese people are not asleep or dreaming; how can we willingly bow our heads and endure the trampling of the imperialists? Recalling the pretexts for the imperialists to conclude and extend unequal treaties, they say that our national construction is young and our legal system is flawed, or that we lack a strong government and unified power. But now our new government is increasingly on the right track, unification has long been achieved, construction is advancing rapidly, and the legal system is fully prepared. The imperialists should have automatically abolished all unequal treaties in good faith to strengthen friendly relations. However, not only do they not plan to do so to fulfill their previous promises, but even when we repeatedly urge them to negotiate, they still use cunning words and sophistry, hesitating and watching. In short, the imperialists believe that repeated wrongs make a right, that the guest can usurp the role of the host, and they still hope to continue their political aggression and extend their economic oppression, maintaining the superior position produced by their superhuman ideology before the Great War. At this time when the imperialists are deeply mired in the illusion of power, if we want to demand the abolition of all unequal treaties in good faith through a friendly and consultative attitude, it is no different from asking a tiger for its skin. We deeply hope that our diplomatic authorities will quickly change their negotiation strategy and resolutely resume revolutionary methods, to avoid being chronically anesthetized by them. Looking at Japan at the end of the last century and the recent examples of Turkey and Siam, all relied on their rationality to strengthen themselves and abolish all unequal treaties. How are we, the new Chinese people, inferior to them, that we cannot automatically abolish them? As the National Assembly is about to open, all our people should unanimously demand that an announcement be made to the outside world to abolish all unequal treaties. Moreover, even on his deathbed, our party leader repeatedly exhorted us to abolish all unequal treaties. We believe that the representatives of the National Assembly have his words still ringing in their ears and will surely follow his instructions. The entire nation will resolutely support them, so that our party's foreign policy can be implemented and the proposals of the National Assembly can be realized. If obstacles arise, the whole country will not hesitate to sever economic ties with them, because we will never tolerate others snoring beside our bed for the sake of our supreme and complete sovereignty. We respectfully announce this, hoping that comrades and compatriots in all regions will rise up and make the same demands, so as to achieve the final goal. It is the fortune of the party and the nation, and the fortune of the Chinese people."

Municipal Government

New Building Tender

Bidding to Open on the Sixteenth of Next Month

The Wuchen Society reports that the Shanghai Municipal Government, since designating the downtown area

Model of the New Municipal Government Building

, has been actively engaged in construction, sparing no effort. Currently, the main arteries running east-west within the area, Sanmin Road and Wuquan Road, have begun construction. The new Municipal Government building will also be put out to tender for construction by the Public Works Bureau starting today. Given the extraordinary scale of the project, it is stipulated that bidders must have substantial capital and experience in undertaking large-scale projects. All drawings and specifications can be obtained from the Public Works Bureau in Maojia Lane, Nanshi, starting on May 4th, for a fee of $25 each, along with a bid deposit of $3,000. Unsuccessful bidders will have their deposit refunded upon return of the drawings. The deadline for collecting drawings is May 15th, and the public bidding will be held at the Public Works Bureau at 2:00 PM on the 16th. A photograph of the model of the new building has been obtained and reproduced above. The exterior style fully preserves our country's inherent flavor, while the opulence and splendor of the entire structure will set a new record for architecture in this city.

Telegram of Congratulations to the Foreign Ministry

Revocation of Consular Jurisdiction by the Netherlands and Denmark

The Foreign Affairs Discussion Group sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, stating: "To His Excellency Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs, Nanjing: We were delighted to learn from the news that the Netherlands and Denmark have revoked consular jurisdiction, restoring our sovereignty and adding luster to our nation. We eagerly anticipate and are overjoyed. We respectfully request that you continue your efforts to complete the work, so that we may see the abolition of unequal treaties at the beginning of the National Assembly. With respectful congratulations, The Foreign Affairs Discussion Group."

Eurasia Aviation Corporation

Invites Guests for Test Flights

May 14th

Eurasia Aviation is scheduled to officially inaugurate its service on May 15th. Before the official inauguration, there will be four test flights each to Shanghai and Manchuria, with free transportation of mail. The test flight results have been excellent. The company's Flight No. 3, which flew from Manchuria to Shanghai the day before yesterday, is scheduled to head north again tomorrow. Therefore, the official inauguration date of May 15th is certain to be realized. The company has also scheduled May 14th, the day before the official inauguration, to invite guests from all walks of life in Shanghai to visit the airfield on Hongqiao Road in western Shanghai and view everything. At that time, the guests will also be invited for an official test flight.

Antipathy Towards American Flour Shipments

The Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Flour Millers Association Sends Telegrams to the Ministries of Finance and Industry

The Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Inland Mechanized Flour Millers Association sent telegrams yesterday to Song Ziwen, Minister of Finance of the National Government, and Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Industry, stating: "We have read in recent Chinese and foreign newspapers that the United States plans to ship surplus flour to China, valued at 20 million yuan, as a form of loan. The government authorities are investigating the actual needs of our country before making a decision. This has caused anxiety among agricultural, commercial, and industrial circles. Last year's harvest was abundant, and the amount of rice and wheat stored in various provinces is still plentiful. The flour produced by various factories this year is already suffering from sluggish sales and huge inventories. Even with low-priced sales, no one is interested. At present, there is no need to import foreign flour. If this becomes a reality, the impact on the rural economy will be immeasurable. The sudden import of large quantities of foreign flour will inevitably exacerbate the problem of surplus domestic flour. Various flour mills will be forced to shut down, which will have a great impact on the livelihoods of workers and the nation's established flour industry. In the past, there was a proposal to ship Japanese rice to our country for low-priced sales, but it was ultimately prevented by bans and public opposition. The American flour situation is the same, so why should we treat one more favorably than the other, leaving a bad reputation? It would be of no benefit to the national economy and the people's livelihood, and the harm would be great for industry and commerce. We respectfully request that you accept this proposal and quickly eliminate this idea to protect commerce, agriculture, and workers. This would be a great service. The Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Inland Mechanized Flour Millers Association."

Publication of the Feetham Report

The Full Text is Divided into Seven Sections

Three Sections Published Today

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement hired Judge Feetham of South Africa as an expert advisor in January of last year to assist the Council in planning construction projects, taking full account of the wishes of the Chinese people and providing reasonable and full protection for the great commercial interests that have already developed in Shanghai. Mr. Feetham spent more than a year in Shanghai conducting investigations and research, and produced a report in seven sections. The content of the first section is an introduction, explaining that his duties are not limited to studying the economic, social, administrative, and political situation of the Shanghai International Settlement and its adjacent areas, but also include the general economic, political, and administrative background of the country, because Shanghai's special problems are closely related to China's general situation. The second section describes the history and conditions of the International Settlement and its governance, stating that the current level of development of various institutions in the International Settlement is the result of gradual evolution. To devise a construction plan for the future of the Settlement, it is necessary to first study the process of this evolution; otherwise, the various problems that need to be solved now cannot be clearly understood. The third section describes the business interests of Shanghai. The fourth section is a statement of findings and comments on political and administrative issues. The fifth section discusses the main issues related to the future of the International Settlement. The sixth section discusses the surface of roads outside the Settlement. The seventh section is a supplement. The sections that are being published now are the first to third sections. A summary of them is published in today's special column of this newspaper, and the remaining sections will be published successively three weeks later.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Protests the Arbitrary Sino-Foreign Litigation Case

Regarding the French Consul's Unilateral Judgment and Detention of the Hulin Manager

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce protested yesterday to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the French Consul's unilateral ruling on the Sino-foreign litigation case of Hulin Silk Weaving Company. The telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing stated: "To His Excellency the Minister of Foreign Affairs, Nanjing: Hulin Silk Weaving Company entrusted Xue Jialai Company, a French merchant, as its exclusive agent in France. In October of last year, the merchant handled a batch of orders worth approximately 1.8 million francs, with a delivery date of the end of December. When the time came, the bills of exchange did not arrive, and the goods could not be shipped. Hulin Company was urged by various weaving factories to fulfill the orders and could only compensate for the losses and return the orders to the original factories. Hulin Company suffered a loss of more than 100,000 yuan. It then temporarily deducted a portion of the commission retained by Xue Jialai Company, amounting to more than 10,000 taels of Huayin. Xue Jialai Company then sued the French Consul, summoning the directors, supervisors, and general manager of the company. After they arrived, the French Consul interrogated them at will in his personal office. Without a formal court hearing or Chinese officials participating in the trial, the French Consul abruptly ruled to detain the manager, Wang Xingsu. According to the Sino-French Treaty of Tianjin and the established practice of the Gongxie over the years, cases involving Chinese and foreign parties should be jointly tried by Chinese officials. The French Consul's actions this time were illegal and exceeded his authority, setting a precedent since the opening of trade. We respectfully request that your ministry investigate and approve a serious protest to the French ambassador to revoke the French Consul's unilateral judgment in this case."

Financial Losses of the Dachang Crew

$50 Per Person... Distribution Scheduled for Today

The financial losses of the crew of the Dahua Company's Dachang ship, which sank in a collision, were completely resolved yesterday. Each deceased crew member will receive a compensation of $300, and each surviving crew member will receive a compensation of $50 for financial losses. Salaries will be paid up to the end of April, and all outstanding salaries for the previous three months will also be paid at the same time. However, the company's finances are not very strong, so they temporarily negotiated with the Huaan Insurance Company to borrow $11,200. This amount will be deducted from the $50,000 insurance fee when the negotiations are completed in the future. Therefore, the Dachang Company's negotiations with the other party must first wait for the crew issues to be resolved before proceeding. Yesterday afternoon, two or thirty members of the Dachang crew, accompanied by the first officer Li Jinqian, went to the company to demand payment of their salaries. Since the funds from Huaan had not arrived, they waited until 3:50 PM before a check was issued by Chengyu Zhuang for $11,200. Because the time for drawing funds had already passed, all the crew's salaries will be paid at the company at 9:00 AM today.

Customs Workers' Strike

The Social Affairs Bureau Orders Resumption of Work First

And Instructs Three Parties to Fulfill the Amended Agreement

While the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Conducts Mediation

Regarding the strike issue of customs workers in this city, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday ordered the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to mediate properly, and ordered the three parties to fulfill the agreement and resume work first. However, it is heard that the Cotton Cloth Trade Association is scheduled to meet tomorrow, and the Customs Workers' Union is scheduled to meet today, to discuss a solution. Details are recorded separately below.

Order to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday issued an order to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, saying, "In order to comply with the matter, it is found that this strike of customs workers, due to the dispute over transportation fees in the cotton cloth industry, has been going on for many days. Yesterday, this Bureau convened a final mediation, and regarding the scope of workers' delivery and the vehicle fee schedule, the representatives of the three parties agreed to amend five articles of the agreement. Only the issue of inspection fees remained unresolved because the parties insisted and repeated persuasion was ineffective. In addition to strictly ordering the customs workers to resume work first, this Bureau will also copy and distribute the records of the agreement already agreed upon and amended by the representatives of the three parties, ordering them to comply with and implement them first. As for who should be responsible for the collection and payment of the inspection fees, it is actually a matter of business responsibility. It is hereby ordered that the Association immediately investigate the usual practices and resolve the matter impartially, so as to eliminate disputes, and that the handling situation be reported for future reference."

Instruction to the Union: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday issued an instruction to the Customs Workers' Union, saying, "Received and noted. It is found that during the mediation convened by this Bureau yesterday, the scope of workers' delivery and the vehicle fee schedule have already been agreed upon by the representatives of the three parties. It is urgent to copy and distribute them immediately, ordering compliance and implementation. As for the issue of inspection fees, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has been ordered to investigate the business responsibility and resolve the matter impartially. In addition to issuing separate orders, you are hereby notified, and you are hereby instructed to instruct all workers to resume work immediately and wait quietly for verification, and not to delay any further, lest you incur blame. This is an important instruction. "It is also heard that the Bureau simultaneously instructed the Cotton Cloth Trade Association and the Customs Association to fulfill the agreement.

Amended Agreement: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, on April 23, separately convened the Transshipment and Customs Association, the Cotton Cloth Trade Association, and the Customs Workers' Union to negotiate the issue of the scope of workers' delivery and vehicle fees, etc. The person in charge of the Social Affairs Bureau solicited the opinions of the representatives of the three parties and compromised to amend the draft agreement, totaling five articles. The full text is recorded below: (1) No matter which factory or warehouse the goods are in, the customs workers shall transport them by vehicle in accordance with the delivery procedures, and each customs house shall issue a delivery receipt for verification. If there is still a situation of refusal to deliver, the Transshipment and Customs Association shall bear full responsibility. (2) From the south to the Ning Shao Old Warehouse and the Dada Warehouse, from the east from Yangjingbang to the Huashun Warehouse, no vehicle fees shall be given for both foreign and domestic cotton cloth. However, for the Huishan, Warehouse, Osaka, and Huangpu warehouses, the Cotton Cloth Association shall pay 25 cents per piece for vehicle fees, and the Transshipment and Customs Association shall pay 15 cents to the workers as transportation fees. (3) Except for the Lihe Warehouse in Suzhou River, no vehicle fees shall be given for both foreign and domestic cotton cloth. For the remaining warehouses along the river, 20 cents per piece shall be paid for foreign cloth, and the goods shall be delivered by the owners at the entrance of the warehouse, and the leverage shall also be borne by the owners. However, the cotton cloth warehouse vehicle fees shall still be handled as usual. (4) For the goods in the foreign warehouses in the concession, everything north to Beijing Road, west to Zhejiang Road, and south to the Edward Road British Concession shall be handled according to the usual delivery methods. No vehicle fees shall be given for both foreign and domestic cotton cloth. (5) For cotton cloth with old vehicle fees, a separate vehicle fee schedule shall be established and paid according to the schedule, without any increase or decrease, or any exceptional demands. (Vehicle Fee Schedule) Yihua coarse cloth 20 cents, coarse twill 35 cents, Hengfeng coarse cloth 20 cents, Yangshupu coarse cloth 20 cents, coarse twill 40 cents, Gongyi coarse cloth 20 cents, Santai coarse cloth 20 cents, fine twill 40 cents, Zhentai coarse cloth 30 cents, Tongxing fine twill 40 cents, fine cloth 40 cents, Dalai coarse cloth 30 cents, Shenxin coarse cloth 20 cents, Neiwa coarse cloth 20 cents, fine cloth 40 cents, Toyota coarse cloth 24 cents, fine cloth 40 cents, Gongda fine cloth 40 cents, fine twill 40 cents, Yongan coarse cloth 24 cents, fine twill 48 cents.

General Assembly of the Association: The Customs Association held a general meeting of representatives of various firms at 2 pm yesterday, chaired by Shi Zhikun, and resolved: (1) From the south to the British Concession Yangjingbang, east to the Huashun Wharf, north to Beijing Road, and west to Zhejiang Road, no vehicle fees shall be given for the delivery of both foreign and domestic cotton cloth. (2) For the delivery of foreign and domestic cotton cloth from Huangpu, Warehouse, Osaka, and Huishan Wharves, the Cotton Cloth Association shall subsidize 25 cents per piece, and the Customs Association shall subsidize the customs houses and workers to negotiate their own terms. (3) With the Lihe Warehouse north of the Suzhou River as the boundary, the Cotton Cloth Association shall subsidize 20 cents per piece for foreign goods in the warehouses west of the boundary, and the Customs Association shall subsidize the customs houses and workers to negotiate their own terms. (5) The Cotton Cloth industry is responsible for collecting wharf fees. (6) The Customs Association shall handle stamp duties with customers themselves. (7) The inspection fees for the box head cloth of this factory shall still be handled in accordance with the regulations, and no more fees shall be charged for the bun white goods in the future. (8) Due to the changing times and the upward trend of living standards, the price list stipulated in this agreement and the prices stipulated in items 2 and 3 may be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for further negotiation. (9) This strike dispute has affected all parties. In the future, brokers will inevitably have a bad impression of the Customs Association, or even infringe on the business behavior of the Customs Association, and the Cotton Cloth Association will be responsible for dissuading them. The following was proposed by the labor side for discussion and was approved by the entire body: (1) Vehicle fees must be paid every Sunday, with a maximum delay of two weeks. (2) In the future, workers must use the union seal to collect vehicle fees from various firms. If there is any private transaction or extra extortion, it has nothing to do with the Customs Workers' Union. (3) If there is a shortage of yards or a lack of codes in the box goods, the handler shall be responsible for handling it himself. If there is any refusal, the Cotton Cloth industry shall be responsible for it, and it shall not involve the Customs Association and the Customs Workers' Union. (4) After the two parties sign the agreement, all parties must abide by the terms of the agreement.

Sanxin Factory to Employ Former Workers

No Regret for the Statement Made Before

More than 4,000 former workers of the Sanxin Textile Factory on Yangshupu Road petitioned the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau because the new factory owner refused to resume work. Now the factory announces that it will start work on the 27th of this month, and registration will begin on the 21st. According to the report of the engineer Wu Shihuai to the labor representative, it is necessary to recruit new workers. As a result, the public is frightened and asks for relief. Moreover, since the factory has been taken over, the former workers should be employed as soon as possible. According to the previous report, it is hereby urgently ordered that you comply with and not allow the staff to deliberately make things difficult, causing disputes. This is an important order."

Order to Zhu Guangcheng: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday issued an order to Zhu Guangcheng, the representative of the capital of the Sanxin Factory, saying, "In order to comply with the matter, (omitted) it is found that when the factory was handed over to the new owner, Zhu Guangcheng, as the representative of the capital, made a responsible statement in advance. Therefore, when the factory starts work now, he should still be responsible for persuading the capital to employ the former workers as soon as possible. In addition to issuing a separate order to the new factory owner Rong Zongjing, you are hereby ordered to comply with and take responsibility for handling it quickly, so as to alleviate the difficulties of the workers. This is an important order."

Japanese Merchants Compete with Chinese Shipping Industry

Organize the Datong Company

Engage in River and Sea Shipping Routes

Named Datong: In the past two years, the Japanese shipping industry has seen an increasing number of businesses in decline, surplus ships, and empty schedules. Several months ago, many Japanese shipowners came to China to engage in activities with our country's shipping industry, willing to lease ships to Chinese merchants, even if they changed their flags. Because no one accepted, the matter was abandoned. Recently, the Japanese shipping industry regards China as the only way to develop its business. However, it is difficult to come to Shanghai to open shipping routes due to our country's recovery of shipping rights. It is heard that the Japanese shipping merchant Tanaka is contacting Chinese merchants with his merchant ships and establishing a new shipping company in Shanghai, using the name of Chinese people to the outside world, while the sovereignty is in the hands of the Japanese. This matter has been under discussion for a long time and has already been established. It is named Datong Shipping Company. The head office is located in Shanghai, and the offices have been leased. It will open for business immediately.

Chinese Manager: In order to maintain its reputation with the outside world, the Japanese hired the Chinese Zhuang Sheng Biao as the manager of the shipping company, responsible for soliciting transportation business. Zhuang is a customs broker and is quite familiar with various merchant groups. He has now been hired. After the shipping route is opened and the ships arrive in Shanghai from Japan, the business will begin immediately.

Shipping Situation: The Japanese shipping merchant Tanaka has more than a dozen ocean-going ships, including those suitable for the Yangtze River route and the North and South Ocean routes. The route is currently being negotiated. Ships must be dispatched to the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River and various coastal ports, but it has not been announced.

Ministry of Industry and Commerce Rectifies Tea Exports

Commodity Inspection Bureau has Submitted Proposed Improvement Plan

Tea has always been a major export commodity of our country. In recent years, foreign sales have plummeted, which is of great importance to the national economy and people's livelihood. Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce paid attention to this when he was the Minister of Industry and Commerce. Since the reorganization of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, he has ordered Director Zou of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry to actively plan improvement methods to seek relief. It is heard that the Bureau has already drafted a concrete plan of action. In addition to requesting the Ministry to establish a Tea Research Institute, a Tea Experiment Field, and overseas propaganda agencies, it also plans to start with inspection first, in order to eliminate the negative aspects and promote fundamental improvements. Regarding the inspection regulations, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce is currently drafting them. Generally, they can be announced around the time the new tea is on the market. The methods of cracking down on tea in various countries all take strict measures. For example, if the quality is poor, the types are mixed, the tea is smeared with paste, mixed with soil and sand, and the tea is colored with damp tea, it is not allowed to be transported for export. If our country adopts strict measures at the beginning, it may have a major impact on this year's trade. Therefore, it has recently been decided to take a compromise approach. In addition to actively cracking down on inferior tea, damp tea, and tea mixed with paste and soil, etc., other teas may be temporarily allowed to be exported after the direct export merchants state their reasons, depending on their customs and needs. As the new tea is about to be on the market, various tea-producing areas are preparing for harvesting and production. If they are not notified early, there may still be fake, substandard, and other teas transported to Shanghai. In order to prevent problems before they occur, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has also been requested to notify the competent authorities of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Jiangxi provinces to instruct the tea merchants and tea farmers in various counties and cities to pay attention to the following points: (1) Tea farmers must harvest and produce early, so that the leaf quality does not harden. (2) When harvesting and producing, the old and tender must be separated, and must not be mixed for harvesting, production, or sale. (3) When tea merchants purchase, they must not smear paste and mix with tail box ash, impurities, and other malpractices. (4) The box boards, tin cans, and other items used for packaging tea leaves must be selected from superior and strong materials, so as to avoid damage, dampness, and other malpractices during the journey, so that tea farmers and tea merchants can prepare early, so as not to feel difficult temporarily. This measure has been adopted and implemented by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce.

Recent Events of the Ministry of Railways

The Ministry of Railways believes that theft of track spikes and other items by thieves damages railway property and endangers the lives of passengers, which is of great importance and cannot be compared with ordinary theft. Since the Criminal Law has provisions on public danger crimes in Articles 197, 198, and 199, it should be strictly followed. In addition to the Ministry's request to the Executive Yuan and the Judicial Yuan to order the courts to severely punish the criminals who steal track spikes and other crimes in accordance with the public danger crimes of the Criminal Law, the Ministry also requested the Ministry of Interior, the provincial governments, and the municipal governments to instruct the Capital Police Department and the public security bureaus to inform them, and ordered the railway administrations and management committees to publicize the provisions of the public danger crimes of the Criminal Law in simple language to the public to raise awareness and maintain railway administration.

The Ministry of Railways received a report from the Longhai Railway Administration stating that the goods stored at various stations are piled up like mountains and cannot be transported out. Moreover, the port is being prepared, and the line will be extended. After the winter of this year, the business will develop and it can be controlled. It is proposed to purchase six Pacific-style locomotives to run passenger cars, so as to free up other large locomotives for freight transportation on the entire line, and to purchase 200 forty-ton all-steel high-side freight cars. The Ministry of Railways has ordered the approval according to the situation. However, it is stated that there are several places in the manual that need to be slightly modified, and they have all been ordered to comply with.

The Ministry of Railways believes that since the Longyan Iron and Coal Mine was taken over by the Ministry in accordance with the order of the Executive Yuan, the northern military affairs have been delayed for years, and the economy is poor, making it difficult to proceed. The Ministry has many complicated affairs to supervise and manage the affairs of the roads under its jurisdiction, and it is difficult to take care of them. Now that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has been established, it is actively planning steel business, and metallurgical talents have been recruited. All the planning matters for the construction of the Longyan Iron and Steel Plant and Mine have been submitted for transfer to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for unified planning and overall planning.

Wood Industry Asks for Reduction of Business Tax Rate

The Chinese and Western Woodware Industry Association yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Tax Rules Research Association, saying, "Dear Sir, yesterday I saw in the newspaper that the business tax rules formulated by the Municipal Finance Bureau of this city will collect 10 per mille from the Western-style wood industry and the rosewood mahogany furniture industry. After reading it, I was shocked. It is found that the business operated by our industry is purchased from the same industry in manufacturing, which is indeed a wholesale nature. Its raw materials, such as rosewood, mahogany, teak, Liu'an, Machili, etc., and its equipment, such as tonic water, paint, glass, chains, hardware, etc., are all subject to business taxes directly and indirectly. Our industry has suffered a lot of secret pain, which is already considerable. Now that it is considered a luxury item and 10 per mille is collected, how can our industry bear this heavy burden? Moreover, at a time when commerce is declining and all things are rising, and expenses are increasing day by day, it is difficult to maintain. If we are taxed at 10 per mille, we will have no hope of escaping the predicament, and we will be frightened. Only the Chamber of Commerce is the leader of commerce, and the rise and fall of business conditions are more accurate than administrative organs. We hereby send a letter to the Chamber of Commerce to check the heavy burden borne by our industry and the situation that we cannot bear it any longer. We hope that you will strongly preside over it and forward it to the Ministry of Finance of the National Government and the Shanghai Municipal Government to sympathize with the difficulties of the business and reduce the tax rate. It is appropriate to collect 2 per mille according to business, so as to relieve the heavy burden and help the business escape the predicament. We sincerely ask for your help."

Rich in Nationality

Zhenru Boy Scouts Fire Fighting Record

At 8:15 pm the night before last (23rd), the material room of the Hexing Company in Caijiazhai, south of Zhenru Station, suddenly caught fire, with thick smoke and flames reaching the sky. The easterly wind was helping the fire, turning it into a prairie fire. Unfortunately, the area is located in the countryside, and firefighting cannot be used. Fortunately, the Boy Scouts of National Jinan University, more than two miles away, quickly caught sight of it and summoned more than 70 Boy Scouts to rush to rescue. Working quickly, the fire was extinguished.

Maid Hanged Herself

Local News Two

Art Student's Suicide

Zou Bin Attempts Suicide by Poisoning Due to Extreme Poverty and News of His Father's Death. Early Rescue May Save Him.

Zou Bin, a student at the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts, attempted suicide by poisoning in his dormitory yesterday morning. He was sent to the hospital by the school authorities for treatment, and it is generally believed that he can be saved. Before taking the poison, Zou wrote more than twenty farewell letters, which he sent to teachers, friends, and a letter to the principal, which stated, "I have been in difficult circumstances for years, and recently suffered the pain of my father's death. After much thought, I have decided to end it all." There was also a final letter containing many complaints, one passage of which said, "Bin was originally a poor scholar, and with the generous assistance of teachers and friends, I was able to study at the Academy of Fine Arts. Now Bin will die before his studies are completed, wasting the cultivation of teachers and friends, and my heart is broken." The reason for Zou's suicide and his circumstances can be gleaned from the above two passages.

Impoverished Family　Zou Bin is 20 years old, from Quxian County, Sichuan. He is a second-year student in the Western Painting Department of the Academy of Fine Arts, Group B. He previously studied at the Sichuan Provincial Middle School. Last summer, he came to Shanghai to apply to the Academy of Fine Arts. Due to his impoverished family, Acting Principal Wang Yuanbo specially allowed him to reduce his tuition to promote his development. Zou was also very hardworking at school and was praised by teachers and friends. A few days ago, his father died of illness in his hometown. When the bad news arrived, Zou Bin looked distraught and his attitude changed drastically. The night before last, at about 10:00 PM, when the lights in the school had been turned off, Zou prepared candles himself and wrote letters alone until dawn.

No Response　Zou lived in dormitory number five. Yesterday morning at about 6:00 AM, Training Director Yu checked dormitory number five and saw that everyone else had gotten up, but Zou was still lying on his bed. He called his name repeatedly without response, which he found strange. He looked around at the table and saw medicine. Fortunately, he was rescued early. He hurriedly asked the school doctor to examine him, who said that he had taken poison. He was immediately sent to the hospital for treatment. It was found that he had swallowed a tranquilizing medicine. Fortunately, he was rescued early. If there are no unexpected changes in the shortest period of time, there should be no danger to his life.

Large Batch of Farewell Letters　Before taking the poison, Zou Bin wrote no fewer than twenty letters to bid farewell to his teachers and friends, all of which were hidden in a drawer. In his letter to Principal Wang, he wrote, "Principal Wang Yuanbo, I am grateful for your repeated special accommodations in registering and attending classes. I am incompetent and have made no progress, failing to live up to your expectations. I have been in difficult circumstances for years, and recently suffered the pain of my father's death. After much thought, I have decided to end it all. The twelve yuan for my sketching fee cannot be returned. Please give it to classmate Zhou Dechang to distribute to my creditors. After my death, do not hold a memorial service at the school, nor do you need to give me any compensation. What I now hope from you is only to supervise classmate Zhou Dechang to carry out my cremation. Classmate Zhou Dechang is always known for his integrity. I hope that because of the problem with his family's funds, you will make special accommodations and allow him to postpone paying the various fees he owes the school. My heart aches terribly, so I will end it here. Respectfully wishing you well, student Zou Bin."

The Truth About Yang Da's Tragic Death

Adulterer Steals Wife, Stages This Tragedy. Body Moved to a Small Ditch After Murder.

Yang Da, a Jiangbei man from the straw shed in the alley east of the Dongyang Silk Factory on Singapore Road in West Shanghai, was suddenly stabbed to death on the evening of the 23rd of this month (the day before yesterday). It was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that the truth of this case is a tragic murder case of an adulterer stealing a wife. The details are recorded below.

Recent Situation of the Deceased　Yang Da, a native of Yancheng, Jiangbei, was about thirty years old. He was married to a woman surnamed Mou, about twenty-four or five years old. The couple originally lived in a straw shed behind Xiaohuayuan on Changan Road in Zhabei. Yang used to work as a runner for a detective in Zhabei. Recently, he made a living pulling a rickshaw. After moving to Singapore Road the day before yesterday, he also pulled a rickshaw for a day.

Cause of Death　According to neighbors there, although his wife, Mou, was very ugly, she was quite promiscuous and had been having an affair with the murderer for several months, meeting secretly in hotels. Although Yang knew about it, he was no match for the situation, so he had to endure it in silence. Recently, his wife's behavior changed drastically, and she often wanted to quarrel with Yang. Yang realized the situation was wrong, so he suddenly forced his wife to move here on the 20th of this month as a temporary measure to avoid trouble. Unexpectedly, the adulterer took this poisonous hand and took his wife away, so as to satisfy his desires.

Course of the Murder　Chen Pan, the second landlord of the straw shed, had a cohabitant named Wang Zhenqing, who introduced Yang Da and his wife to rent a room on the 20th. They moved in immediately. The second landlord, seeing that the couple was not getting along well and often quarreled, did not even ask her wife's name, which was He. Unexpectedly, after living there for only two days, at about 11:00 PM on the 23rd of this month, while she was fast asleep, several people suddenly broke down the door and violently beat Yang Da. The second landlord, Chen Pan, was awakened by the sound and was about to shout when the six or seven murderers each held sharp knives and iron bars, frightening her into silence. Seeing this, she trembled and had to wrap herself in the quilt. After the murderers stabbed Yang to death, they dragged the body to a nearby small river ditch and fled with Yang's wife. The next morning at about 4:00 AM, the second landlord got up to check and saw blood flowing everywhere on the ground. She searched by the ditch and found Yang's body naked on the ground. She then reported it to the Sixth District Police Station.

Landlord's Testimony　After Director Ren received the report, he immediately sent officers to investigate the body. He found a knife wound on the temple, a bar wound on the back of the neck, and an iron bar inserted into the flesh of the left waist, about three inches long, which had not been pulled out. He then found a police whistle, three keys, a diary, six cards, a disciple's post, a promissory note, and an account book in his room. He also detained Wang Zhenqing, the introducer, at the station. After Director Ren questioned the second landlord Chen Pan, she confessed that she was 40 years old, from Yancheng, and lived in a straw shed next to the silk factory. Wang Zhenqing, her cohabitant, introduced Yang Da and his wife to rent the house on the 20th of this month, and it had only been two days. However, the man and woman had not been in harmony since entering the house. Unexpectedly, last night, she suddenly heard someone break down the door and violently beat Yang. She planned to shout, but six or seven people held sharp knives and frightened her into silence. She had to hide in the quilt. It was not until she got up at 4:00 this morning that she saw Yang's body had been thrown in the ditch, with blood flowing everywhere, which was unbearable to look at. His wife had disappeared, etc. Wang Zhenqing also confessed that he was 30 years old, from Yancheng, and lived at the same address. Yang Da previously lived in a straw shed behind Xiaohuayuan on Changan Road in Zhabei. He met him in April last year. Two days ago, he suddenly asked him to find a house, so he introduced him to rent here. He did not know the reason for his murder, etc. After Director Ren obtained the confession, he immediately prepared a document and sent it to the court for trial, as the case concerned a murder.

The Second Volume, Third Issue of "Ren Wen" Is Published On Schedule.

Scholars regard it as a reference tool and call it the best publication of modern historical materials, "Ren Wen," and it is published on schedule. The index of the main items in this issue contains a total of 88 magazines and 1,700 selected items. The notes include "Miscellaneous Notes" by an anonymous person, recording events in Beijing during the Shunzhi period of the early Qing Dynasty. For the convenience of readers, the journal has repeatedly reprinted each issue of the first volume. Special Article

Mr. Feith's Report

Abstract Translation of the First to Third Compilations (I)

Note: This article is not a detailed summary of Mr. Feith's report. The entire report is too long, and its content cannot be fully summarized within such a small scope. The purpose of Mr. Feith's article is only to reveal the general nature of the contents of the first volume. For the sake of brevity, many important arguments in the original book must be either completely omitted or briefly described. Those who wish to see the whole picture and know its detailed contents should seek it in the full text of the report. The original text of the first volume of the report can be purchased directly from Bifa Foreign Firm and Sino-American Book Company for one yuan per copy. The Chinese translation is being translated.

Report: Divided into seven compilations as follows: First Compilation, Introduction; Second Compilation, History and Status of the Public Concession and its Governance; Third Compilation, Shanghai Business Interests; Fourth Compilation, Statements and Comments on Political and Administrative Issues; Fifth Compilation, Major Issues Related to the Future of the Public Concession; Sixth Compilation, Roads and Ground Outside the Concession; Seventh Compilation, Supplement. Currently, only the reports of the first to third compilations are published. The remaining compilations have not yet been submitted and will be published later.

Preface: A letter from Mr. Feith to the Chairman of the Board of Directors of the工部局 (Shanghai Municipal Council) on April 25, 1931, was added in abstract and published at the beginning of the report as a preface as follows: The 工部局 allowed me to fully investigate freely in accordance with my own method, and at the same time, I am grateful for the assistance given to my request. The assistance of the board of directors and the members of the board is extremely valuable. I have found the assistance of them and the assistance of a majority of people outside the bureau who have nothing to do with the affairs of the bureau to be the same. The topics I should pay attention to and the sources I should visit are entirely up to me. To make a fair and unbiased discussion of the main facts about the situation in the concession, this discussion must include the past or present that I freely determine. After the materials are collected, I am free to deal with the judgment according to my own method. The full responsibility for the content of the report is therefore borne solely by me. Only I am bound by the chapters in this volume and the volumes that will be continued, and no one else. Regarding the attitude of those who study my report, I would like to briefly state what I hope for on the left. Those who are familiar with the situation in Shanghai will not fail to recognize the difficulties and complexities of the problems that I have been entrusted to deal with. Almost half of my requests for assistance have been generously granted because of the deep sympathy for the difficulties of my position. In terms of the facts of this kind of difficulty, it may allow me to make a request to the readers, whether in Shanghai or not. I would like to ask the readers to listen patiently so that I can finish my words, and to read the report with not only patience but also an open mind. The report is published in installments. The reason has been mentioned. Readers must be particularly tolerant of this. Chinese and foreign residents within the public concession, as well as other people in China and elsewhere, have expressed patience and waited quietly for the report to be completed. I hope that they will be patient for a while and not draw conclusions about the views and suggestions in the volumes that are yet to be published based on what is described in this volume. Although what is described in this volume is regarded as an "investigation," I know that it is still far from a complete investigation. When discussing political issues related to the future, there are various facts that need to be discussed. Most of these facts will be left to be published in the fifth compilation that specializes in this issue. When preparing the report, I deeply felt that the greatest service I could hope to do for all the citizens of the public concession was to make a just study of all the problems in the intense disputes to the best of my ability. When the problem is studied justly in its true sense, there must be remarks that are not welcomed by this party or that party. Part of what is said may not be tolerated by the opinions of some foreigners, and another part of what is said may not be accepted by the opinions of some Chinese people. I would like to sincerely ask all parties concerned not to be angry about what I say. If I were to fear offending the intentions of this party or that party, I would not present the various relevant reasons that must be taken into account. I would have failed to fulfill the duties unanimously requested by the工部局, which represents all the residents of the area. My responsibility is very clear, that is, not only to avoid discussing the problems I have seen in order to make the report I have prepared acceptable to the general public, but also to leave aside the main reasons that are regarded as inappropriate from the point of view of this party or that party. As mentioned earlier, the report has to be long. I would like to specially ask the readers not to read each section separately from its context, or to only seize a certain word or sentence, because this kind of word or sentence may contain a completely unintentional offense. Please wait until you have finished reading the entire report. The first volume now published can be regarded as a complete article.

First Compilation: This compilation is the introduction to the report. The directors of the 工部局 unanimously invited Mr. Feith to take charge of the investigation. The origin, scope, and method of all investigations are stated in the introduction. After arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Feith soon sent a letter to the Chairman of the Board of Directors of the 工部局 on January 15, 1930, explaining the scope of his powers. This letter has also been quoted in the introduction. As far as the letter shows, the duties that the 工部局 asked Mr. Feith to take on were "to be an advisor to the 工部局 and to assist the Bureau in planning and building, to fully consider the wishes of the Chinese people, and at the same time to give reasonable and adequate protection to the great business interests gathered in Shanghai." The report mentions that, in terms of this scope of powers, the scope of the investigation is very broad, so the nature of his duties is explained as follows: Therefore, my duties are not only limited to the study of the economic, social, administrative, and political conditions of the Shanghai Public Concession and the locations adjacent to the Concession, but also to know the outline of the current situation of the environment to which Shanghai belongs, in other words, the general economic, political, and administrative background of the country, which must also be known. Shanghai's special problems must be observed from this background, and then the truth and proportion of each problem can be known. If we do not first know the general situation of China, we cannot make the proposed Shanghai governance system and the direction of national progress form a suitable relationship, nor can we plan and carry out any proposed reforms, and give the economic interests involved the necessary protection. However, this common background must always be kept in mind, and my preliminary work is of course to study Shanghai itself and, in particular, to understand the nature and scope of Shanghai's industry and commerce, so that it can be a solid foundation for the commercial center, as well as the characteristics of the current governance system of the Public Concession. For any plan for the future of the Public Concession, the Chinese and foreign communities within the area certainly have the right to express their opinions first. I must also visit, understand, and consider these opinions clearly. The procedures for the investigation have been summarized in the report, and the various sources of information obtained have also been mentioned. In addition, it has been pointed out that, in terms of the current situation in Shanghai, it is difficult to conduct a public investigation. Compared with most other central locations in China, Shanghai has more freedom of discussion. The main reason is that it is convenient to publish opinions on current affairs issues in Western newspapers. However, even in Shanghai, it is difficult for foreigners to freely and publicly discuss political issues, and it is probably impossible for Chinese people. The report also said that the Chamber of Commerce, the Bankers Association, other organizations representing commercial interests, and certain Chinese organizations have given valuable statements directly or indirectly related to political issues and allowed them to be published. However, most of the people who gave their opinions personally made it clear that when mentioning the opinions of these people, the person who expressed the opinions should not be disclosed. All the assistance and suggestions obtained from all parties under this restriction are worthy of gratitude.

Second Compilation: The general nature of the contents of this compilation is as follows: The reason why the existing institutions of the Public Concession can develop to the present level is due to gradual evolution. To prepare a construction plan for the future of the Concession, we must first study the process of this evolution; otherwise, the various problems that need to be solved at present will not be clear, that is, we will not be able to understand the true relationship of each problem. Therefore, the content of the second compilation is, as its title states, to trace its history and describe its status. The first chapter of the second compilation briefly describes the current situation of Shanghai and its administrative area. The second chapter describes the origin and development of the Public Concession. It mentions that, at the beginning of its establishment, the Concession was originally regarded as a residence for British residents, but the British authorities did not insist that it was only for British residents, so most people from other countries could enjoy equal rights in the Concession and could participate equally in political affairs. The Concession, which belongs to this kind of nature, has important differences from the concession area exclusively managed by one country. Its name is Concession instead of Shanghai Concession (the French Concession is not included), which also has important consequences. The report mentions the following important points: The Public Concession in Shanghai was initially just a small place, originally designated as a residence for British residents. Later, it gradually expanded. The concessions of other treaty ports in China are separated from each other and intersect with each other, while the Public Concession in Shanghai is of a mixed nature, forming a single autonomous group. Most people of various countries within the area are governed by the civil municipal system, and the limited supervisory powers are retained, so that it belongs to the consular corps of various countries that enjoy extraterritoriality and have their own people living in the area, and not to the consul of any one country. The organizational characteristics of the foreign community in Shanghai are like this, and the large number of countries related to the Shanghai Public Concession has made the historical situation in Shanghai complex and made progress slower and more difficult than concessions managed by only one foreign country. However, the result of the union can add strength, increase independent methods, and enable all foreigners to not only undertake municipal administration, but also to expand its activities on a larger scale than areas managed separately in other locations, and can develop a habit of international cooperation. This habit has its own special value and may prove to be increasingly important in the future.
