Free Talk

World Miscellany

— Seafarer

In the year 1929. Men in London are once again embracing the fashion of wearing beards. Many can't wait for their beards to grow, so they are attaching fake beards to their faces. As a result, wig makers in the West End of London are busy rushing to produce fake beards.

In the South American country of Argentina, cricket is popular every summer. Cricket is as fervently loved as football in the winter. Last year, they initiated international cricket matches, competing successively with Chile, Brazil, England, and other countries.

The Hunter Museum of the Royal College of Surgeons in England has a collection of 3,000 skulls from various eras and countries, all unique. It is said that this museum has the finest skull collection in the world.

King Boris of Bulgaria is the poorest king in Europe. He only has an annual income of six thousand pounds. He also has to support his sister, Princess Eudoxia. She is content with just one new dress a year.

In Hyde Park, London, there is a famous lake called Serpentine. Starting in the summer of 1930, men and women will be allowed to swim together.

Anecdotes of the King Addicted to Drama

— Cicada Slough

Is drama entertainment or art? Neither is an issue here. Take my old friend, the King Addicted to Drama. It would be wrong to praise his politics or promote his literature. The King simply loves to watch plays. When he was a student in Shanghai, he didn't miss a single play, except when he had classes. If he had money, he would buy a seat in the stalls; if not, he would stand at the back. He was a true believer in watching plays, rain or shine. Moreover, he was sincerely there to watch the plays, not to promote the actors or write critical reviews. He went to every theater, knew every actor. This was enough to qualify him as addicted to drama. However, because of his sacred and august position, ever since he graduated from Shanghai, he was hired in Liaoning, first as a teacher, then as a secretary. Whenever there was a long summer vacation, or when he went to Beijing on official business, the King was always found in the theaters of Dashilan. The King once said, "One must watch plays in Beijing to appreciate the beauty of Beijing opera." As for the King's time in Fengtian, he watched plays every single day.

When Grand Marshal Zhang opened his headquarters in Beiping, the King, with his high position, was attended to by many. But the King's addiction to watching plays remained unchanged. He felt unwell if he didn't see a play for a day. Thus, friends in Beijing and elsewhere called him the King Addicted to Drama. Even Grand Marshal Zhang called him by this name.

Grand Marshal Zhang had advisors like clouds and soldiers like rain. Whenever he had free time, they would sit around him, discussing politics or history. The Grand Marshal would doze off, as if he heard nothing. Only the King's words, which were about thirty years of theater history, and whose origins were all from personal experience, without making friends in the theater world or writing articles for newspapers, would capture his attention. The King's evidence was the playbills from the past thirty years. Beijing originally had no playbills; he had his own handwritten diary. So the King's stories were about watching plays, not about the theater world. That's why the Grand Marshal would stroke his mustache and smile when the King spoke. Since the King graduated and left Shanghai, it has been twenty-five years. And these twenty-five years in Liaoning, Beiping, Tianjin, Shandong, and Guangdong have all been filled with playbills. Even during the five years he studied in Shanghai, traveling to Nanjing, Zhenjiang, and Suzhou, he always watched plays. Therefore, compiling these playbills together has already filled two large boxes.

The King is now sixty years old. His family urged him to return, so he resigned from Deputy Commander Zhang's office. Deputy Commander Zhang, valuing their old friendship, gifted him with 30,000 gold pieces as retirement funds and sent an adjutant to accompany him south. He has been in Shanghai for three days, visiting various theaters. The scenery is vaguely familiar, but the landscape has changed.

Yesterday, he paid me a special visit. Seeing each other felt like a lifetime had passed. I thought that the anecdotes of the King Addicted to Drama should be passed down in Shanghai as a model for playgoers. Therefore, I specially wrote this article to publicize it.

Special Announcement

Starting from May 1st, this publication will establish a "Fiction Rotary Club." Famous writers Tianxu Wosheng, Wang Dun'gen, Bao Tianxiao, Jiang Hongjiao, Xu Zhuodai, Yao Suifeng, Zhang Henshui, Cheng Xiaoqing, and Cheng Zhanlu will take turns writing various short stories. Each story will be about ten thousand words, all being works of both emotion and refinement. Readers, please pay attention.

Anecdotes of the Alleyways

— Drunken Fool

Society is like a devil's den, and alleyways are full of jokes. Recently, the red rain adds to the sorrow, and the green windows are boring. I casually record a few anecdotes for your amusement.

A sudden, uninvited moving crew. One morning, a moving truck arrived at the entrance of an alleyway and stopped abruptly. Soon, a man and a woman led several workers straight into a certain family's house. They began to move out the rosewood furniture and other items in a flurry. They even went to the nearby police station to report the relocation. They loaded the items onto the truck and sped away. Meanwhile, the wife of the family hid in a neighbor's house. At the time, housemates and neighbors who witnessed this strange scene were all baffled. Later, when they questioned the wife, she tearfully said that her husband had a gambling addiction, and she had repeatedly warned him without success. Last night, he gambled at a gambling den in Beili. At first, he won a little, but then he lost heavily. In addition to emptying his pockets, he still owed over a thousand gold pieces. The people in the den were intimidating, and they forced him to write a promissory note, promising to repay the debt with the rosewood furniture in his house. That's why they came to move it today, she said. Everyone who heard this sighed at the wife's misfortune. With her home stripped bare, she couldn't stay there for a day. The next day, she packed up the remaining items and clothes and quietly moved away with her husband, no one knew where.

Everyone, please look at the model. In the front alleyway, there is a certain family, husband and wife. They live in a detached Western-style house. The wife is only seventeen years old, still with a childish air. She always greets people with a smile and is adorably naive. A few days ago, because of the heat, she was taking a bath behind closed doors in a room downstairs. A shop assistant from a neighboring store learned about it and peeped through the window. Soon, more and more people gathered, drawn by the rumors. The wife was very embarrassed. Suddenly, she stood up naked and declared to the crowd, "I might as well let you see your fill. It doesn't matter." The crowd was startled and scattered like birds and beasts. The wife happily told others, "This is the strategy of retreating to advance. It's my wonderful plan to withdraw the troops." Those who heard this laughed heartily.

Ask the one who tied the bell to untie it. A neighbor, Mr. A, works on a certain ship and is rarely at home. His wife couldn't bear the loneliness and had an affair with Mr. B, who lived in the same house. Mr. B was a widower, and their secret affair had been going on for a long time. One day, while they were in the midst of their tryst, Mr. A suddenly returned from outside. Mr. B hurriedly hid, and Mr. A didn't know anything. The next day, Mr. B, in a state of panic, developed a fever and chills, turning into typhoid fever. Mr. B's mother was very worried and said that the illness was caused by the wife. She launched a war of recrimination. The wife was also in the wrong and offered to pay for the medical expenses. Every day, the wife embraced Mr. B and rode in a rickshaw together to see the doctor. The scene was very amusing. Onlookers even thought they were a couple.

One Evening of Song and Dance

— Address

Last night, I watched the film "Border Province Swordsman" at the Summer Coolidge Theater. As the play ended and I was about to leave, I suddenly heard countless young girls making noise backstage. Curious, I watched as the audience left, and I stood alone to observe and inquire with a waiter. I learned that it was the actors of the Liwa Dance Troupe. The waiter said that the troupe would be performing at the theater starting on the 25th, so they were holding their final costume rehearsal on stage tonight. I have always been fond of singing and dancing, and the name "Liwa" had already deeply impressed me. Curious about what it was like, I got the consent of a certain gentleman from the troupe, so I was able to return to my seat and feast my eyes.

The dance drama rehearsed by the troupe consisted of four acts: "Youth," "Moonlit Heart," "Paired Shadows," and "Goddess Luo." In "Youth," there were 32 actors on stage. The costumes were quite novel, and the plot was also subtle. The most exciting part was the final scene, a dance performed by all 32 people. Every movement of their hands and feet was in rhythm and perfectly synchronized. This could not have been achieved in just a few days. The plot and lyrics of "Moonlit Heart" were quite exceptional. A man and a woman stood together in a suspended crescent moon, surrounded by stars, beautiful and enchanting. Watching the heartbroken girl singing a sad song under the moon made people tearful. In "Paired Shadows," there were 18 actors on stage. The first segment was roughly about ordinary men from all over the world wooing an extraordinary woman. In the end, they were all disappointed. The second segment was about ordinary women from all over the world wooing an extraordinary man. They were also all disappointed. Finally, a pair of extraordinary people loved each other. The ordinary men and women all sympathized with each other and loved each other. The intention of the play seemed to be that "the most perfect marriage in the world is only the paired shadows in a mirror frame." In "Goddess Luo," there were 65 actors on stage. The costumes and scenery were the most luxurious and novel in the play. I heard a certain gentleman from the troupe say that the cost of one hat was about a hundred US dollars. The final scene, with 65 people dancing and singing together, was solemn and magnificent, truly a grand event in the world of song and dance.

Let Me Also Talk About Tuina

— Shi Min

I once read the accounts of the origins and development of Tuina by Yingchuan Qiushui and other gentlemen. The references to classics and records were extremely detailed and comprehensive. I have not even glimpsed the doorway to the art of Tuina, so I dare not offer reckless praise. The following account is based on stories passed down by elders and is only meant to aid conversation. According to legend, the art of Tuina considers One-Finger Zen to be the orthodox school. Its strength is sufficient to cure all diseases, but unfortunately, only one in a hundred people who study it achieves great success. During the transition between the Ming and Qing dynasties, there was a recluse whose name has been lost, an old scholar who was learned and skilled in many arts. He had a unique approach to Tuina, creating many new methods that surpassed the ancients. After the dynasty change, he devoted himself even more to this art, hand-copying several exquisite volumes. These volumes gathered the essence of Bodhidharma's One-Finger Zen and incorporated his own views. The illustrations were detailed and the explanations were extremely thorough. After the recluse died, this secret book was scattered among the people. During the Jiaqing era, it eventually fell into the hands of a salt merchant named Huang in Jiangdu. It is said that Huang obtained this book simply because the calligraphy was powerful and the illustrations in the section on Qi Observation and the semi-nude figures in the gynecology section were in the style of famous artists. Therefore, he spent money to buy it, viewing it as an ordinary antique. Later, Huang's family declined. A member of the family named Aisheng, who was studying medicine, found the book in a box. He was overjoyed and studied it day and night, gaining much insight. Later, he became famous for his One-Finger Zen Tuina. He is now Dr. Huang Hanru, who hangs his pot at South Chengdu Road in Shanghai. Hanru's wife, Hanyun, and his son, Yizhao, both inherited his teachings. It is said that they owe much to this secret book.

A Piece of Paper Worth Ten Thousand Gold

— Dream

Japanese literary giant Kikuchi Kan has produced a body of work that is the envy of many. His literary reputation is well-known. The payment for his articles is calculated by the line, and the value of a piece of paper is considerable. Even a single line or word is valued accordingly by booksellers. The news of this spread and became a beautiful story. It is unexpected that there is something similar. A photograph can be awarded up to ten thousand US dollars. These events, shining one after another, are truly extraordinary.

The initiator of this award is Kodak, a company with a reputation for reliability. They started a photography competition two years ago. This year, they are making even greater efforts, launching a world photography competition with a prize of one hundred thousand yuan. However, only amateur photographers are allowed to participate, and the awards are divided into sixty levels to increase interest. There are also many awards for the Chinese side, including six major category awards, provincial and regional awards, and a national grand prize of one thousand yuan. The first-prize photos from each category will be collected and sent to Geneva for evaluation. The first-prize winner will receive one thousand US dollars. The best photo in the world will be awarded ten thousand US dollars and a sculpture of the goddess of photography. Thus, a single photograph can continuously receive awards amounting to more than ten thousand gold pieces. In today's increasingly urgent commercial warfare and fierce competition, many are trying to win by surprise in order to make their businesses far-reaching. Kodak's move is a way to take advantage of the situation. The business can be controlled. Throwing away ten thousand gold is indeed generous.

Indian Travel Notes (34)

— Linghua

Today, several Chinese monks, returning from worshipping the Buddha on the mountains of North India to the south, passed through Calcutta and were about to return to Rangoon. They also stayed at the Guanyin Temple in the Siyi Hall of the Chinese city. They came to the Mahayana Buddhist Association to see the Buddha's relics. I had never seen them before in my life. Today, I also respectfully viewed them. The secretary of the Mahayana Buddhist Association, Xin Hanjun, reverently opened the altar for viewing. They were in a small pagoda. The pagoda was golden. It was a sunny afternoon at one o'clock. In the Buddhist hall upstairs, the sunlight was shining directly in. I and three others faced east to view them. One piece was the Buddha's bone, weighing about half a tael. It was slightly black from age. Next to it, one grain was what is called a relic, about the size of a wheat grain, perfectly round, pure white in color. The sunlight reflected off it, with a slight glow. We respectfully bowed to it. There was a monk who was called a living Buddha who was fond of bowing. He would bow upon hearing a good word. He placed the small pagoda on his head and chanted mantras for about ten minutes. He also placed it on the heads of the three of us, saying that it could directly connect us to the wisdom of the Buddha. I once heard people say that Buddha's relics can emit light and can fly away on their own, decreasing or increasing in size. It is also said that their color varies depending on the person who sees them. Those who are advanced see golden light, those who are average see white light, and those who are inferior see black. Seven or eight tenths of my brain is material science, and I do not deny it. Spiritually, I still dare not determine whether this statement conforms to material science or whether the Buddha truly has supernatural powers and the color of the relics varies according to the level of the person. I remember ten years ago, when Okuma Shigenobu was prime minister of Japan, the King of Siam gave Buddha's relics to Japan. Okuma initiated a donation of 1.1 million from the cabinet to build a pagoda to store them. I don't know what happened to that matter. Or what happened after the earthquake.

I asked Xin Hanjun whether these relics were not stored in Ceylon, but in a certain place in India. The relics are different for Buddhas, Bodhisattvas, and Arhats. They are not bones, but the essence of the Dharma body of those who cultivate the Tao, like the Taoists' saying of achieving the elixir. According to people, all those who cultivate the Tao can obtain relics after cremation. After the Buddha's death, his bones were cremated and divided into several sections, and the relics were divided into several. The kings of various countries took them and built pagodas to store them. This matter is detailed in the Nirvana Sutra. Apart from mythology, I dare not easily believe it. In short, at least the Buddha was a great philosophical teacher. In his life, he lived a simple life to save sentient beings. In his death, he cremated his corpse to be distributed to relatives and disciples, crushing his bones and powdering his body in the hope of influencing the ignorance of sentient beings and leading them to correct wisdom. Liberation is like this, and it is enough. Mozi praised those who wore out their scalps and wore down their heels to benefit the world. The Buddha crushed his bones and cremated his body to leave a memory. His kindness and compassion for people were great. However, the Nirvana Sutra records that the kings of various countries almost used force to compete for the Buddha's bones. It is truly laughable. Fortunately, I am a commoner, so I can view the Buddha's bones without interference. If I were an emperor, I would not necessarily be able to see the Buddha's bones. Mr. Han Yu also wrote a memorial to argue for them, adding to the troubles. It can be seen that emperors are not as free as commoners.

On the 21st, I read a book called "Calcutta," written by Hassan Suprawardy and narrated by Seferoldwa. It tells of the English's first conquest of India, which is something we like to hear. I extracted a few points below. Briefly, the first to arrive in India in 1625 were the Portuguese and the Dutch, who operated shops at the mouth of the Hooghly River, which is the mouth of the Ganges. Thirty years later, in 1658, the English began to trade. Their trading company was called the East India Company. At this time, it was near the 17th century. English trade was very prosperous here. The small village where they operated was called Hooghly, which was the base for the English's development. Times create heroes. A manager in the company named Senior Agent Jot Charnock (translated as Ke Leifei in the past, which is probably the Cantonese pronunciation) arrived in India in 1682. Based on this company's mechanism, he created a unified Indian government. Charnock was the creator of the English conquest of India.

Gold Prices Rise Again

Rising More Than Seven Taels Compared to Yesterday

No Many Units, People's Hearts Are Solid. Yesterday, the 24th, gold prices rebounded and rose again, with slight changes. There were fluctuations of two or three taels to five or six taels. The morning market fluctuated around 730 taels, and the afternoon was often above 33 taels. The total market had a review of 15 taels, and finally rose more than 7 taels. However, the exchange rate slightly reversed, seemingly showing a potential for easing. It once posted a long position, which was opposite to the gold market. Therefore, English gold arbitrage was suitable, only leaving about 20 taels, especially close in the afternoon, only about 16 or 17 taels, which was very different from before. It is likely that the foreign silver market has risen and is not affected by the slight drop in gold prices. In the future, buying will be strong, because the bill of exchange seems to be tight, so it has escaped the 30 tael mark. Later, because sellers were not lonely and the bill of exchange weakened, English gold loosened by 1.25, so it dropped by five or six taels. After the market, buyers were agile and presented an upward trend, nearly 40 taels. Afterwards, the bill of exchange did not see improvement, and it was frustrated again, but the result was mild, totaling 36 or 37 taels. In short, there are not many units, and people's hearts are solid here.

The Yarn and Cotton Market Presents a Quiet and Firm Atmosphere

The yarn market is slightly firm, but the trend is still soft. This is because the overseas cotton yarn situation is very weak, so retail investors are mostly bearish. The overall situation is still flat. However, the gold price is still firm, and the market can be slightly hardened. There is no large-scale development in spot yarn sales, but scattered transactions are still uninterrupted. The auction yarn price has risen due to the Sichuan gang covering short positions. The buying interest in the market is slightly tight, but the major players are still inactive. For the time being, it is still a flat situation.

Grain and Rice Market: Firm in the Morning, Flat in the Afternoon

Zhabei: Yesterday, there were about 20 boats arriving on the inner roads. In the early morning, the opening of Northern Japonica rice was tight due to the lingering effects of the previous day's overcast rain. The intention to enter was also active at this time, so the price once turned firm near the corner. However, by midday, the sky cleared up, and the buying interest suddenly weakened, so the market became flat. As a result, all grades of white Japonica rice were the same as the closing price of the previous day. The supply of Bo Dao rice was not strong, and the sales market shifted with the Japonica rice market, so there was little upward or downward movement. Yang Xian rice and Du Bu Xian rice seemed active at the initial opening, but they soon settled down. There were not many transactions throughout the day, and the situation was stable. White Yuan rice shipments were rare, and sales became brisk, raising the price by one jiao and a half.

Hunan: Yesterday, there were about 20 boats arriving from the river. Sales in the street were still acceptable. The Jibai Japonica rice on the west and north roads had a very promising market atmosphere in the morning, with the market rising to the left of the corner. In the afternoon, the sky cleared, and the mood turned flat, with transactions becoming weak. However, the price remained firm. The overall opening market today will inevitably decline slightly, which is not strange. On the southern road, the arrival and sales of thin early rice were both matched, and the market rose by nearly a foot. The Yang Du Jian market presented a hovering pattern. Since the goods were scarce, the price also rose or fell by only a few fen. The Yin Hua rice supply and sales were both dry, and sales suddenly improved, so the market increased by one or two jiao.

Auction Flour Turns Weak Again

Yesterday's flour market: After the opening in the morning and afternoon, the prices for each month generally turned flat and weak again. Because the foreign wheat quote decreased by two or three jiao, everyone's perception inevitably focused on one side. The market price for this month had weakened, but the manufacturers' purchases made it feel stable. As for the long-term months, because the actual sales gangs were inactive and the foreign atmosphere returned to a state of oversupply, it could no longer be determined whether foreign wheat would be stable. The import of foreign flour was inevitable. Therefore, this guest's gangs were all in a state of quietness. The market atmosphere became depressed. The future trend may re-enter a dangerous situation. As a result, the current month was unchanged, May was down by a small 7 li and a half, June and July were down by a small 1 fen, August was down by a small 5 li, and September was down by a small 7 li and a half.

Wheat Futures Market Weakens

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning, the markets for each month showed a near-stable and far-weakening trend. Although the foreign wheat was quoted down by a small two or three jiao, the weather was still overcast, so most people did not see any impulse. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, the markets for each month had gradually changed. Because the current month was approaching delivery, the ratio of long and short positions was already perceived as more supply than demand. Because the cargo release was very smooth, and only one or two manufacturers were receiving, the market situation became very weak. The current month could not be suppressed, and the long-term months naturally could not stand firm. It was said that the spot wheat in each warehouse was indeed heavily accumulated (it was heard that Tai Run Bank arrived again with nearly 100,000 bags yesterday). As a result, the current month fell by 5 fen compared to the previous day, May fell by 4 fen, June fell by 3 fen, July fell by 5 fen, August fell by 3 fen, and September fell by 2 fen.

Dried and Preserved Goods: Jinshan Branches Suddenly Rise

Jinshan branches had been slow-moving, and the market had reached 33 or 34 taels. According to news from the production area, last year's winter was too cold, and this spring's flowering was very sparse. From the current phenomenon, this year's new harvest will inevitably be poor, and the current stock is not much. Since there are fewer arrivals, yesterday's market suddenly trended up. Ordinary goods rose by about 3 taels, and high-quality goods rose to more than 40 taels. Retail prices also rose accordingly.

Oil Market: White Tung Oil Sales Decline

For the past five or six years, white tung oil has relied heavily on export trade, averaging over 50,000 tons each year, with 4,000 to 5,000 tons per month going to foreign traders. The market's momentum can be imagined. Since the autumn and winter of the year before last, the European and American businesses have gradually declined due to the impact of high gold prices. According to statistics from the old year, only over 2,000 tons were exported throughout the year. The reason for this is that many American paint companies were restricted by finance and were mostly closed down, resulting in a sharp reduction in usage. The majority of China's tung oil exports are to the United States, followed by Europe. Since the United States reduced procurement, China's exports were severely impacted. Therefore, last year's market price plummeted. In previous years, the average was always around 30 taels, but it has fallen to around 20 taels now, oscillating back and forth, a difference of 10 taels compared to two years ago. Both quantity and price are now incomparable. In the past two weeks, according to the so-called Han telegram, it was once sold for 20 taels and 5 qian and 7 qian and a half. However, each transaction was only dozens of tons, up to 100 to 200 tons. The days of thousands of tons at a time are gone, and the market's vigorous momentum is only a historical relic. Yesterday, according to Han Xun, 35 tons were sold, and the price was 20 taels and 2 qian in foreign regulations. Foreign firms only had sporadic transactions, and the market was only stable, with nothing exciting to report. It was heard that traders were opening进客货计襄桐at 18 taels and 2 qian客盘. Sichuan tung oil is arriving today, and wholesale prices are between 18 taels and 2 qian and 18 taels. The Zhejiang tung oil purchased by local firms in the city was at a maximum of 31 yuan per load a week ago, but has recently fallen to 30 yuan. Domestic sales will enter the silkworm season soon and gradually decline.
